Q: Which is more plausible, X or Y, as the sentence that will come between R and S?
R: Jane was a professor teaching piano to students.
S: Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book.
X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day.
A: Let's think step by step.First, we know that Jane was a professor teaching piano to students. This means that she had students who were taking lessons from her. 

Next, we have two options: X and Y. 

Option X states that two of Jane's students were early for their lessons. This is plausible because it is common for students to arrive early for their lessons, especially if they are eager to learn or want to practice before their lesson. 

Option Y states that none of Jane's students had a lesson that day. This is less plausible because if Jane was a professor teaching piano to students, it is unlikely that none of her students would have a lesson on a given day. 

Therefore, option X is more plausible as the sentence that will come between R and S. 
Therefore, the answer is X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
